  28. First, I bought this off walmart.com, because at the time, with rebates, it was about $40 cheaper. I don't think that's the case at the time of writing this review (about 2 months after I bought the shaver).<br /><br />Prior to buying this shaver, I had an older model Braun (similar foil system to 790) that I've had since the early 2000's. I kept with this shaver for so long because my chest and neck are sensitive, so once I find a razor that doesn't constantly give me razor bumps in those areas, I stick with it. I was hesitant about upgrading to a newer model, and had read lots of reviews about the 790cc model being good for people with sensitive skin.<br /><br />From day one, I've had no issues with this razor. To shave (as braun recommends) I always hold my skin taught, and with this shaver, I hardly have to put any pressure at all to shave (compared to my older model). I have been using this for almost 2 months now, with excellent results. It is able to get a close shave that lasts throughout the day. Of the 2 months that I have been using this, I've only gotten razor burn on my chest maybe 3 or 4 times, and have not had any on my neck (compared to my old shaver of razor burn on chest & neck at least 1-2 times per week). I couldn't be happier with those results. I am someone who needs to shave every day, and on average I shave 6-7 days a week. The cleaner cartridge lasted me about 5 weeks before I had my first change (which was simple, and quick). As for actual cleaning, it is simple and automated, you just push a button to initiate the cleaning cycle (which seems to last around 30-40 minutes, although the actual cleaning part where the shaver turns on and off, and makes noise lasts maybe 5-10 minutes, and I suspect the rest of the time is drying the shaver, which is silent).<br /><br />I've noticed a couple of flaws so far, with regards to the cleaning process, both of which are minor. First, the self cleaning process seems to do a good job at cleaning the razor blades, and foil, but does not clean the outer part of the foil (the plastic parts of either side of the foils). Not a big deal, occasionally, simply wetting a finger and wiping it across the plastic parts cleans it off easily. Second, I've noticed that within the &#34;well&#34; that the shaver hangs upside down in, after a cleaning process, there is some left over hair that does not get washed down. Doesn't seem to affect anything, the shaver still seems clean, runs smoothly the next use, and the next cleaning cycle works just fine. It doesn't seem to ever build up, so I'm guessing some of the hair doesn't get washed down and gets stuck there, then the next cleaning cycle washes that down, but some of the newly shaved hair gets stuck in its place. Again, it doesn't seem to affect anything, and never seems to increase in amount. I guess i was just surprised when I first discovered this (about 1 month into using the shaver). Thirdly, if you use the pop-up sideburns shaver part, that is not cleaned by the auto-self-cleaner, and has to be manually done. I rarely use this, so its not too much a concern to me.or blades, and foil, but does not clean the outer part of the foil (the plastic parts of either side of the foils).   111. I have had this shaver for about 4 months now, this is my first electric razor. I have a very sensitive face that is subject to in grown hairs. I shave every weekday with this razor. It is plenty fast. at the rate I was going through razors, this thing should have itself paid off. Shaving the neck, particularly just below my jaw line, proves to be difficult. If you ensure you're going directly against the grain, combined with a couple of passes, you will get those pesky hairs wiped out. squaring off the sideburns is easy with the trimmer (which works very well), but doesn't shave close enough for me. more difficult with the main shaving head. My only real gripe is with the cleaning base, it is noisy and I am not too confident in the job it does. Im sure it sanitizes well, but doesn't get all the hair off. The noise might not be an issue for you, but I shave before my wife is up, so I had to move my unit to the guest bathroom. really I think a bottle of isopropyl alcohol next to the shaver could alleviate the need for the cleaning base. I think a better job can be done quickly by popping off the head, rinsing it with hot water, spraying with alcohol, brushing off the motor output area with the provided brush, and popping the head back on. If I could do it over again, I would pass on the cleaning base. refill cartridges aren't breaking the bank, but for what I think they are composed of (alcohol, scent, and maybe some anti corrosive lubricants), they are too expensive.<br />Don't let my negative paragraph steer you away from this razor, I agree with the videos supporting this and its competition are on point, you can't really go wrong. Just pass on the fancy cleaning base, because thats all it is, fancy.

If you have hair which grows from various directions on a patch of skin, you have to pass the razor over the same spot from many directions to get it all. Even when you pass over it from the correct direction the razor might not get it on the first pass. Also, if my beard is longer than 3-4mm I need to do a pass with the trimmer accessory first otherwise it is a painful yank-fest.<br />2. Cleaning is a nuisance. I tried cleaning it manually and the built-in display never indicates it is clean unless I run the stand's cleaning cycle. I assume the electronics are dumb and just count how long it has been used vs when it was last cleaned using the machine.<br /><br />Overall I was pleased at how close a shave I could get (with some practice), but disappointed in how many passes over my face I have to do. It is much better than relying on disposable razors when I'm traveling so I'm happy with my purchase. As an added bonus it is much easier on my face than a blade.

  427. I've purchased both 7-series Braun (from Amazon) and 5-series (Costco) and been comparing them for a few weeks.<br />Both are fine shavers, and either is a good buy imo. The main difference I found between the two is the subjective &#34;look and feel&#34; - the sturdy, heavy and solid 7-series feels like a premium product compared the 5-series which feels &#34;plasticy&#34; in comparison (only in comparison - don't get me wrong, it's a finely made product).<br />7-series base is also an improvement over the 5-series - holds a shaver more positively, has better contact with the charging terminals on the shaver, less likely to loose contact due to the agitation during the cleaning cycles.<br /><br />In terms of shaving quality, I found them indistinguishable. Although the 7-series has a more powerful, higher-frequency linear motor and what looks like a more advanced shaving block as compared to the &#34;conventional&#34; 5-series, this did not translate into a closer shave, a faster shave, or less skin irritation. My wife couldn't tell a difference over multiple rounds of comparative shaves.<br /><br />The real downside of the 7-series, however, is its pop-up trimmer. It is adequate for using on the sideburns, but really clumsy for the moustache (my case), as the shaving head obscures the view in the mirror. 5-series has a much more convenient slide-out trimmer that works well in all situations I used it.<br /><br />I very much like the look and feel of the 7-series, its gizmos like the extra indicator lights and a somewhat more advanced base, but in terms of &#34;core&#34; functionality it adds no value over the 5-series. And it has a worse trimmer than the 5.<br />So I think that the 7 is a good choice if you're buying it as a gift and want to make a great impression, but if you're buying it for yourself, save some $$ and go for series 5.<br /><br />P.S. I was disappointed that none of the new shavers offered an improvement over my 12-year-old Braun 7505 in terms ofspeed or quality of the shave. No point in upgrading whatsoever if your old & trusted shaver is still working.

  443. BACKGROUND: I purchased the Braun Series 7 Model 797cc which is identical to the 790cc except for being specified in the manual as suitable for use in the shower which was a requirement for me. I bought this unit yesterday and used it just last night. It may be useful to point out that my beard is second to none in terms of being thick and wiry. I cannot even grow it out because it irritates my skin as though I have steel wool on my face anytime I touch it or lay my face on my pillow at night. Thus I must shave every couple of days (3 at the outside) or things quickly get uncomfortable. After days of research I found out that I needed the most powerful motor available for whatever model and brand I was going to buy to deal with my beard. I've had experience with lesser models of Braun in years past and they have performed OK but still would give me razor burn. Middle of the road Panasonics performed the same but the actual shave quality was not up to the level of a similar quality Braun model. I've been switching back and forth between my aging inexpensive Panasonic wet/dry and the Gillette Power Fusion blade (which is excellent) but decided to step up to a new electric and after much reading of reviews decided on the Braun Series 7 Model 797cc. As much based on my personal experience with their products over the years as the many available reviews. REVIEW: The bottom line is that this shaver is hands down the best electric shaver I've used in the 62 years I've been shaving. Now understand that I've only used it once and that was last night when I shaved a 3 day growth. So this is not a longevity/ruggedness report. Amazingly, given the extra time it took to shave 3 days growth I experienced utterly zero trace of skin irritation. I do mean ZERO. This tool just seemed to vibrate the beard off rather than cutting it off. Because it was my first go with this razor and the fact that my beard had 3 days growth I expected that given my face was not used to this shaver i expected at least some problems in the irritation department. As I said I had no irritation whatsoever AND the best shave with an electric shaver ever. I would go so far as to say that it is easily 95% of what one would expect from a blade shave. I shaved last night, nearly 20 hours ago and my beard has only grown in as much as it does the day after a blade shave, if that. The lithium-ion battery level indicator was barely changed following the shave so if for some reason I didn't have power available to charge the shaver I expect that I'd be able to get quite a few shaves out of it even with my heavy beard. The cleaning mechanism looks to be decently designed. I tested it out ONCE and it appears to work as advertised. It comes with one cleaning cartridge which is a sturdy plastic container holding the liquid cleaner which is largely alcohol. These cartridges last about 8 weeks assuming one uses the cleaner every other day or so. They cost about $5 each so that's about $2.50/month. I'm thinking even though the instructions say not to mix your own cleaning solution that I will do it anyway and see how it works. A guy on Youtube (https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=liMN23Xqcis) gives some great instructions on how to do this and where to get a reasonable cleaning mixture to add to some alcohol and thus cut the cost. The other obvious ongoing cost is the replacement of the cutter/comb head which doesn't last forever and is recommended to be replaced every 18 months. If things change further down the road with this shaver I will update my review but based on my personal experience with Braun products I would indeed be quite surprised to discover it to be a dud. UPDATE 10-17-2014: I've been working this shaver hard the past 10 days and to get a shave quite close to that of a razor it does take some time. This used to be a major problem for me with electric shavers and in particular with the Norelco rotary types which would rub my skin raw trying to get a reasonably close shave. This shaver continues to allow me to spend as much time as I want to get the job done without the irritation. My heavy beard makes it necessary to work at it some after the bulk of the beard is shaved off. That is, trying to get as many of the &#34;straggler hairs&#34; as possible. I've discovered that doing the bulk of the shaving dry then hitting the shower with a dab of Gillette shave cream to clean up the stray hairs works best. Obviously everybody's beard is different and some shavers will work fine for one person and not so much for others. If your shaving experiences have been similar to mine then you have a much better than even chance of getting the same excellent performance as I from this shaver. 04-09-2015 UPDATE: The bottom line is that after 6 months of use this is STILL the best electric shaver I've had in 50+ years of shaving. I don't miss the blade which is used for 15 years after giving up on electric shavers altogether. The cleaning system is also excellent and since it can be used in the shower I wash it in there and then run it through Braun's cleanins system. That alone makes the solution last 6 months instead of just one month.

  577. This is about as good as it gets when shaving with an electric shaver and I've had them all (Panasonic 8243A, Norelco Sensotouch 3D 1280, Norelco AT895, Braun Series 7 760). Why so many shavers? I have a passion for electric shavers and when a new shaver comes out, I generally have to try it. I've been shaving now for 50 years so this is not something I come to without experience. I read some negative reviews and invariably they reveal one thing: ignorance of the shaving process so permit me to share a bit of what I've learned.<br /><br />First off, all modern electric shavers are going to deliver the goods, albeit some may be more irritating to the face/neck than others. In general you will find that it takes at least three weeks for your face to adjust to the new shaver so persevere and do not go back and forth with your older razor/shaver. Shave against the grain and using a foil like this Braun, shave in straight motions and at 90 degrees to the face. There is no need for any pre-shave but it is important to shave in relatively dry conditions in order to achieve good glide with the shaver. I find that shaving a half hour after my shower provides the best overall shave, however if that is not an option, shave before showering. With a Braun you press the shaver moderately against the face unlike a Norelco which requires a very light touch. If you press too hard you're going to end up irritating your face and neck. Finally, shave until your face &#34;looks&#34; clean rather than &#34;feels&#34; smooth. The problem with the latter is that you'll continue to shave too long in order to achieve that baby butt smoothness and this will result in irritation. Eventually as your face adjusts to the new shaver you can lengthen the shave and shave to that smooth feel, about ten minutes.<br /><br />The Braun is a superb example of German craftsmanship. It has the right heft to the shaver and there is no plasticky feel to it as there is with a Panasonic. The noise level is moderate (i.e. not as quiet as the Norelco and not as noisy as the Panasonic). It will take either the Smart or the Opti foil cartridges but I think you will find the Opti foil to deliver a better shave. Because the shaver's blades cannot be accessed due to the cartridge nature, the cleaning module is a must. Yes, it can be rinsed under the tap but that really doesn't provide the best cleaning NOR does it lubricate the shaver's cutters. You can, of course, use the oil that Braun provides (a drop rubbed onto the foil once a week) but the cleaning module is a much more elegant solution. Some people argue that using the cleaning module is too expensive but here is my take on that. Three cleaning cartridges run about $20 so a single will run about $7 and last you one month &#34;if&#34; you use the cleaning module on a daily basis. Isn't your face worth a couple of coffees a month? When I pick up my shaver each morning, it is like a brand new shaver... clean, smelling fresh, properly sanitized. You can, of course, use the cleaning module once or twice a week and recap the cartridge to prevent evaporation thereby extending the life of the cartridge. That is for you to decide what is best for you and your budget.<br /><br />Overall, I could not be happier with my new Braun 790 cc.

To cut down on the expense of the Braun cleaning cartridges, I tried a larger refill but the liquid doesn't seem to clean or lubricate it as well as the Braun cartridges. I found I get the best cleaning from an ultrasonic cleaner and then use some electric shaver lubricant I had. UPDATE 10/2014: I have stopped using the cleaning base. I plug the power cord from the base directly into the shaver for charging. The charge on the batteries seems to last forever. I don't even bother with the ultrasonic cleaner anymore. I just remove the head, blast it with hot water in the kitchen sink, let it dry and put electric shaver lubricant on it before I use it. Of course the indicator always says it needs cleaning because the base is what resets it. I just make sure to clean it once a week.

  796. Although the braun 790cc has a high price tag it is worth it if you suffer from sensitive skin like I do. Cartridge shaving and rotary electric razors would leave my skin red and beaten by the time it was all done. I now use this razor on the extra sensitive mode and it is FAR superior to any electric razor I've owned before(Remington/ Panasonic rotary shavers). It shaves my face and neck very efficiently with no irritation. But keep in mind a good prep and post shave is key if you have sensitive skin. Some tips I have learned are: shave 1+ hours after waking up in the morning, use a small amount of baby powder 10 minutes before you start the shave to get skin bone dry, during this 10 minute intermission massage the facial hair against the grain with your hands to lift hairs off the surface of the skin, shave your trouble area first (mine is the neck) and be as light and gentle as you can while pressing the razor to the skin. I shave against the grain in slow long strokes then I go at a very slight angle with the same pressure to get bbs skin with this razor. Some users have suggested that shaving every day will give you the best shave but I disagree. For me, allowing the hair to grow for 2-3 days is best and I believe it's because the hair is now long enough to be efficiently guided into the foil.(when I shave every day a lot of hairs are just passed over by the blade) also, a good post shave is KEY for sensitive skin. I use Nivea mens sensitive post shave balm that I got at Walmart for 6$ IT IS THE BEST I have tried far too many post shave balms and this one is light years ahead of them all. It ensures no irritation, smells fantastic but not over powering, and it actually slows the growth rate of my facial hair. I know that sounds crazy but it really does, I can now go 3 days with no shaving and my facial hair will be the same as if I didn't shave for 1 day. Trust me, get it. The razor takes a little getting used to so give it 1 month before you decide to return it. For me, the only reason I bought this razor was for the shave quality so that is all that I will review today. I have had no problems with other aspects of the razor and cleaning system so far.
